Bhd 100% MRCB Environment Sdn Bhd 55% 9 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Chief executive officer’s statement Mohamed Razeek Hussain MAricar Chief Executive Officer On behalf of the Board of Directors, I am pleased to present this year’s MRCB Sustainability Report which highlights our contribution to sustainable development and the effects that our actions have on our main stakeholder groups – customers, shareholders, employees, business partners, society and the environment at large. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 10 Last year was significant for MRCB. We committed to delivering great performance as one of the leading developers of residential, commercial and industrial properties in Malaysia. I am happy to say that notwithstanding difficult economic circumstances, the strategic direction and vision of the Group has helped to deliver both our business and Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR) objectives. For the year 2009, we achieved a turnover of RM921.6 million which is a 17 % increase from the previous financial period. Our achievements were recognised when MRCB won three categories of the ACCA Malaysia Sustainability Reporting Awards 2009 (ACCA MaSRA) – “Best Environmental Performance Report”, “Special Mention – Assurance Approach” and was a finalist for the whole award. MRCB is amongst the top two finalists at the Prime Minister’s CSR Award 2009 for Culture and Heritage and was also selected as a finalist at the StarBiz Corporate Responsibility Awards 2009 in the Marketplace Category. MRCB continues to be recognised by National Annual Corporate Report Awards (NACRA) in 2009 and has won the Silver Award for Best Corporate Social Responsibility Reporting. MRCB’s property business at Sooka Sentral has been recognised by the Malaysian Chapter of the International Real Estate Federation (FIABCI) Property Award 2009 in the Purpose-Built category. Our former Group Managing Director, Shahril Ridza Ridzuan was named Property CEO of the Year by FIABCI Malaysia. This shows a true accomplishment of MRCB as a Group. MRCB is represented as a committee member of the Malaysian chapter of the United Nations Global Compact (UNGC) in keeping with our aim of adopting international standards for our CSR programmes and vision. The goal is to incorporate all the 10 UNGC principles on human rights, labour rights, environmental sustainability and anti-corruption into the Company’s operations and strategies and to report on their implementation. We support and pledge to continue to observe the 10 universal principles on human rights, labour rights, environmental sustainability and anti-corruption. 11 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 384 Sentral Commitment Towards Better Disclosure and Transparent Reporting We have continued to maintain our excellent performance in reporting by achieving Application Level A+ in accordance with the Global Reporting Initiative (GRI-G3) framework for Sustainability Reporting. The independent assessment by GRI in Amsterdam confirms that MRCB has reported on all required core indicators under GRI-G3 which measures disclosure and transparent practices in business. In this reporting period, we have been able to provide additional information in areas previously under-reported including disclosure of significant emissions levels, environmental impacts of transporting products, the governance system of MRCB environmental programmes, lists of other sustainability management systems and social and environmental accounting data. Environmental Initiatives MRCB is a leader in the field of environmental engineering in Malaysia and has been involved in beach, river and coastline restoration. We work with the Government in helping to avert environmental crises in line with the Ninth Malaysia Plan. MRCB continues to play an active role in mitigating floods, rehabilitation, the management of drainage and combating other environmental issues. In 2009, MRCB completed its Lot G rehabilitation project on Pulau Tioman which cost a total of RM132 million. A detailed analysis of the impact of this project has been performed and the results disclosed in the Environment section of this report. We have extended our efforts by incorporating environmental issues into other business divisions. The initiative now covers our construction management projects which are included as Key Performance Indicators. MRCB is committed to playing its role as a Malaysian company by contributing to Malaysia’s Green Objectives. We are proud to lead Malaysia’s own Green Building Index for existing and future development projects through several green building initiatives and best practices such as the Leadership in Energy and Environment Design (LEED) certification issued by the US Green Building Council; Building and Construction Authority (BCA) Green Mark of Singapore and the Green Building Index (GBI) of Malaysia. This strategy has been implemented in all new projects in our iconic landmark Kuala Lumpur Sentral development – 348 Sentral, Lot G and Lot E. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 12 The Group has also implemented an Environmental Management We are committed to monitoring the environmental performance Plan (EMP) to monitor the environmental impact of our operations. of the buildings under our management and are pleased to We have built an Environmental Management System (EMS) report the continuing success of our systems at Stesen Sentral to manage all aspects of environmental performance including Kuala Lumpur, the capital city’s main public transport hub. We emissions, marine and water quality, material use and the have achieved a 20.3% reduction in energy consumption in 2009 reduction of energy use and waste. This report places significant which surpasses our annual target of 5%. emphasis on the impact of our projects and the results are disclosed in the Environment section of this Report. Climate Change MRCB’s rehabilitation projects require its sub-contractors We continue to support ‘Earth Hour’ by switching off nonto comply with Malaysian Environmental Legislations and essential lights and other electrical appliances for one hour Guidelines as produced by the Department of Environment and to raise the awareness of climate change. We also used a other relevant authorities. poster awareness campaign with WWF Malaysia to encourage tenants in our buildings to support the event. This event was managed by MRCB at 1 Sentral, Sooka Sentral, Plaza Sentral, Stesen Sentral, and Plaza Alam Sentral. In 2009, we conducted a Greenhouse Gas (GHG) study for the first time. The purpose of this study is to help develop a GHG reduction strategy based on our current carbon emissions. Corporate Citizenship I am also pleased to report that we have intensified our efforts to create shared value for society by focusing our Corporate Responsibility projects on Community, Marketplace and Environment. In 2009, we have invested just over RM1.5 million in our community projects. This reinforces our commitment to create shared value not only for our shareholders but also the community at large. MRCB is committed to nurturing the tangible relationship between us and our stakeholders and our CSR initiatives are integrated with our business and brand strategy. Six schools were adopted under the MRCB PINTAR programme in 2009. The schools are SK La Salle 1 and SK La Salle 2, in Brickfields, Kuala Lumpur, SK Tebrau Bakar Batu in Johor Bahru and SK Bagan Jermal and SK Kampong Jawa in Penang. This is the final year of the three-year PINTAR adoption programme for two of the schools. I am delighted with the positive results and feedback this programme has received. We believe that children are our future and it is our responsibility to provide them with the best standards in their academic journey. We increased our efforts to enrich the communities in which we operate and have taken mitigation measures in order to minimise the negative impact and accentuate the positive effects our construction activities have on local communities. For example, we comply with and exceed the national regulations on noise levels, vibration, dust and other environmental issues. 13 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report In the Marketplace, we continued to promote good business practices across the Corporation. Good Corporate Responsibility is the essence of our success. We will do our utmost to play our role as a model Corporate Citizen. Workplace Initiatives Due recognition must be given to our employees who have worked hard to create profit and ensure other financial indicators are healthy. We are balancing our short and long term objectives in order to deliver steady and sustainable growth. This ensures a strong return for our shareholders despite a challenging operating environment. In 2009 we continued to invest in staff training programmes to develop skills further and prepare for greater challenges in the workplace. We recognise employees as a core asset to the company and The challenges of addressing increasing demand in believe in lifelong learning for them. MRCB has continued emerging markets and the forces of convergence across to invest in human capital development to strengthen their global environmental concerns, such as climate change, are employability. The Board encourages communications at all all significant issues for our business. We are committed to levels to help our employees think and act as one cohesive engaging with our direct and indirect stakeholders proactively organisation in the best interests of the company. through our Corporate Communications team which is the champion in upholding CSR issues with support from senior management and respective division heads. As part of our future agenda, we will focus more attention on positioning the MRCB Foundation strategically within the Group. We will also conduct a comprehensive employee and stakeholder satisfaction survey that was identified as the gap in this year’s performance. Acknowledgement On behalf of the board, I would like to express my deepest appreciation to the management and staff for their dedication, commitment and contribution and to our customers for their continued support. CSR in Challenging Times As always, we hope you find our report useful and informative and we appreciate your comments and feedback which are The current year will be one of the most challenging to date. valuable to us in developing our future initiatives in line with We are confident that with the commitment of our people, the expectations of our stakeholders. strict internal controls and good management, we will be able to meet the challenges ahead. I am just as pleased to report that the Group has continued to achieve strong top and bottom line growth. This is testament to the sound policies and strategies in place. We are in full support of the Government’s effort to promote ethical standards within companies. We strive to improve our sustainability initiatives to complement these efforts. Assess The Potential Impact of Issues and Their Importance to Stakeholders Our stakeholder groups include both internal and external stakeholders. The largest internal stakeholder group is our employees. Board Independence and Effectiveness i. The Company continues to ensure that there is clear separation between the Board and the Executive in order to achieve a balance of power and authority as prescribed by international best practices. ii. In this aspect, the role of the Chairman (who is non-executive) and other Board members are always kept separate from the role of GMD/CEO, who is principally responsible for making and implementing operational decisions. iii. In the absence of the Chairman, the most senior independent director, Dato’ Ahmad Ibnihajar, will chair the Board meetings. iv. The Board’s effectiveness is further enhanced with the set up of 5 Committees of the Board. The Terms of Reference of each committee is set out in pages 131 to 134 in the MRCB 2009 Annual Report. In these committees, each director’s individual skill sets and expertise are tapped. The committees were set up to support and complement the Board’s decision-making process, since more detailed review and study of strategic issues can be done at the Committee level. Nevertheless, the Board retains the ultimate responsibility for decision-making. Board Committees Audit Committee The Audit Committee Report is set out on pages 153 to 156 of the MRCB 2009 Annual Report. Executive Committee In a continuous effort to improve itself for effective leadership and management of the Company, the Board had on 17 November 2005 established an Executive Committee (EXCO), which main functions are: i) To guide the Management in the implementation of the GLC Transformation Initiatives; ii) To review and recommend the annual business plan and budget of the Company to the Board for approval; iii) To consider and review significant and/or major issues relating to any business direction of the Company; iv) Deliberate on all major business transactions and issues relating to the Company that require the EXCO’s or Board’s approval in line with the approved Limits of Authority. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 20 Nomination Committee The Code endorses, as best practice, a formal procedure for appointment to the Board, with a Nomination Committee making recommendations to the Board. In line with this, the Nomination Committee (“NC”) was established on 31 October 2001. The NC’s terms of reference include: i) Identifying and recommending new nominees to the Board and committees of the Board of MRCB, and nominees to the Boards of its subsidiaries. All decisions and appointments are made by the respective Boards after considering the recommendation of the NC; ii) Assisting the Board, committees of the Board and directors in assessing overall effectiveness on an on going basis; and iii) Assisting the Board in periodically reviewing its required mix of skills and experience and other qualities that non-executive directors should bring to the Board. The NC shall meet at least once a year, and a quorum of three (3) is required to convene the meeting. Remuneration Committee In line with the the recommendations of the Code, a Remuneration Committee (“RC”) was set up on 31 October 2001. The terms of reference of the RC are: i) To determine and recommend to the Board the framework or broad policy for the remuneration packages of the Chairman of the Board, the GMD/CEO and other senior management personnel it is designated to consider; ii) To establish a formal and transparent procedure for developing a policy on the total individual remuneration package of the GMD/CEO and other designated senior management personnel including, where appropriate, bonuses, incentives and share options; iii) To design the remuneration package for GMD/CEO and other designated senior management personnel with the aim of attracting and retaining high-calibre senior management personnel who will deliver success for shareholders and high standards of service for customers, while having due regard to the business environment in which the Company operates. Once formulated, the remuneration package is recommended to the Board for approval; iv) To review and recommend to the Board improvements (if any) on GMD/CEO and designated senior management personnel’s remuneration policy and package, and any other issues relating to benefits of those designated senior management personnel on an annual basis; v) To review any major changes in employee benefit structures throughout the Company, and where appropriate recommend to the Board for adoption; vi) To review and recommend to the Board for adoption the framework for the Company’s annual incentive scheme. The framework for the annual incentive scheme may include: • Merit increment • Merit bonus • Incentives Employee Share Option Scheme (ESOS) Committee The ESOS Committee was set up to ensure that the implementation of the ESOS scheme was administered fairly in accordance with the Company by-laws of the ESOS Scheme approved by Shareholders. During the year under review one ESOS Committee meeting was held to discuss 2009 ESOS allocations proposed to employees of the Company. * A complete Corporate Governance section can be found in MRCB’s Annual Report 2009. 21 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report MRCB foundation BOARD OF TRUSTEES Chairman Tan Sri Azlan Zainol Chairman, MRCB Members Shahril Ridza Ridzuan Board of Director, MRCB Dato’ Anthony@Firdauz Bujang (Chief Executive Officer NSTP) (Independent) Wan Radzly Abdullah Wan Ali Chief Financial Officer, Bank CIMB Niaga (Independent) OPERATION TEAM Secretary: Mohd Noor Rahim YahayaCompany Secretary Treasurer: Chong Chin Ann Chief Financial Officer Operation: Mohaini Mohd Yusof General Manager and Head of Corporate Communications Department CORPORATE MEMBERS Malaysian Resources Corporation Berhad Kuala Lumpur Sentral Sdn Bhd MRCB Environment Sdn Bhd The MRCB Foundation was successfully incorporated in December 2009 as a non-profit organisation to carry out both Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR) and philanthropic activities. The Foundation will become the vehicle for a more focused and systematic approach to the MRCB Group’s CSR approach. This will replace the current structure of decentralised CSR activities. The MRCB Foundation is an ideal vehicle to combine resources and allow better Group activities. It will encourage MRCB’s shareholders and employees to become responsible corporate citizens by contributing to communities in a systematic way within its areas of business. This central focus allows MRCB and its shareholders to work towards creating a better future, as well as encouraging our customers, investors, employees, suppliers, communities and stakeholders in becoming a caring community. The objectives are: (1) To foster, develop and improve education of all kinds approved under the education laws of Malaysia for the benefit of local communities and schools in selected areas, all for the welfare and for the betterment and enrichment of the Malaysian society irrespective of race, religion and creed. (2) To organise activities, including fund raising events, providing funds and in-kind contributions for the promotion of the arts and for the relief of human suffering (natural disasters), all for the welfare of the public and for the betterment and enrichment of the Malaysian society irrespective of race, religion or creed. (3) To receive and administer funds from time to time for any charitable purposes for the welfare of the public and for the betterment and enrichment of Malaysian society irrespective of race, religion or creed. Beach Rehabilitation Works Using “Pressure Equalisation Module (PEM)” at Teluk Tekek, Tioman Island, Pahang Darul Makmur Located off Malaysia’s east coast in the South China Sea, Tioman Island is one of Malaysia’s most popular tourist destinations, an area of natural beauty and high biodiversity value. In 2009, MRCB successfully completed the project on Tioman Island, “Mereka membina dan menyiapkan projek pemulihan pantai dengan menggunakan ‘Pressure Equalisation Module’ (PEM)” which was implemented at Teluk Tekek. The erosion that occurred previously at these areas has affected the biodiversity of the island and damaged local infrastructure. MRCB’s PEM system is reported to have overcome the problem of coastal erosion by undertaking various forms of coastal defence and beach nourishment. The beach is also rehabilitated for the enhancement of tourism and recreational value. The rehabilitation of a badly polluted river was also carried out using rubbish traps to prevent pollution and other waste from reaching the sea. MRCB also conducted an environmental awareness campaign on the island to highlight the importance of cleanliness, recycling and environmental preservation. This included awareness seminars with the local inhabitants, especially those with businesses along the river, beaches and coasts. 27 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report This project is a prescribed activity under Activity 17 (d) of the The pressure equalisation modules lower the groundwater Environmental Quality (Prescribed Activities) (Environmental level in the coastal profile from high to low tide. Over time the new materials in the coastal profile become Our EMP has been prepared by an environmental consultant increasingly coarse, due to a higher speed of the underlying to address potential significant environmental impacts that water in the coast profile. may arise during the construction period. Several potential environmental impacts arising from this project include: air, noise and vibration; marine and river water quality; marine life and coral health; management of waste; and health and safety. We are proud to report that no injuries occurred during this reporting period. MRCB Pressure Equalisation Module (PEM) System Our Pressure Equalisation Module (PEM) system is radically different to the dredging, sand nourishment and groynes building methods previously employed for coastal protection. The PEM System has a low impact on the aesthetics of the beach area and avoids disfiguring it with boulders. The PEM System is an environmentally friendly approach to coastal protection. Conceptual outline of the PEM system (equilibrium profile) Pressure equalisation modules are vertical filters that are placed in a matrix along the coastline. Due to gravity, there is considerable groundwater pressure from the land side. The sea water in the swash zone percolates through the sand and runs back into the sea “on top” of the groundwater discharge area. This advances the erosion process that occurs as the sea water runs back in the swash zone. The filters equalise the pressure in the groundwater zone which increases the circulation of seawater in the coastal profile.This promotes the sedimentation of materials on the coastal profile. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 28 Environmental Impacts of Transporting Materials MRCB has identified significant environmental impacts from the transportation of construction materials and precast seawall section. Mitigation / Prevention Measures Impacts Identified • Coral reef areas marked with buoys • Physical damage to corals due to • Dedicated access routes for vessels and impact by barges and vessels demarcated with buoys • Spills and leaks of fuels and chemicals from • Anchoring on corals was strictly prohibited storage tanks and drums • Skid tanks and drums are secured within • Spill of sand from the barges into the sea during an impervious spill container rough seas or overloading • Barge traffic was suspended during rough sea • Navigation hazard due to movement conditions to avoid accidents of barges and boats • Material and fuel was carefully handled with spill containment facilities Biodiversity Study In 2005, a total of 60 marine water samples were taken at locations within the project site and at control points outside Project site. At each location, water samples were taken from the surface, mid-depth and the bottom. The water samples were preserved and sent to an accredited laboratory for analysis. Environment performance is monitored on a monthly basis by the appointed Environmental Consultant, ERE Consulting Sdn Bhd. Near shore corals were totally absent; instead sand and coral rubble were the prevailing substrates. Coral reefs are geological structures of calcium carbonate built over time by tiny living organism called polyps. Coral reefs, which are sometimes referred to as the underwater rainforests, are the world’s most biologically diverse ecosystems. In conjunction with the rehabilitation of Teluk Tekek beach in Pulau Tioman, a Detailed Environmental Impact Assessment (DEIA) was conducted to assess the existing coral reef status prior to recommending necessary mitigation measures. A total of 153 reef fish species from 36 families and 84 general of reef fishes were recorded for the whole study. Other species recorded include Drupella, which has strong feeding preferences for branching corals; Stichopus chloronotus, which is highly valued in commercial trade; and Stichopus herrmanni variegates, which is traditionally known for its medical value. Three species of giant clams were also recorded; Tridacna maxima, Tridacna squamosa and Tridacna crocea which are all protected under the Fisheries Act 1985. We have conducted a detailed impact analysis study during pre-construction and post-construction of the project. Design and Build Works for the Rehabilitation of Pahang River Mouth and Surrounding Beach Areas The project site is located approximately 10km from Pekan town and approximately 40 km from Kuantan, the capital of Pahang. The main objectives of the Pahang river mouth improvement works are to overcome the siltation problems in order to enable the safe navigation of fishing vessels to and from the Lembaga Kemajuan Ikan Malaysia (LKIM) complex, to provide adequate navigation channels, berthing and mooring areas as well as shelter against waves especially during the monsoon period. Akreditasi Makmal Malaysia (SKMM) Climate Change Climate Change presents potential risks and opportunities to our business in the medium and long term. MRCB has responded by starting the Green Building Project initiative. The concept of green building brings together a vast array of practices and techniques to reduce and ultimately eliminate the impacts of buildings on the environment and human health. Modern initiatives call for an integrated and synergistic management approach during construction and completion. This approach integrates the building life-cycle with each green practice and technique employed to create a synergy between the developer, operator and users. The reduction of natural resources used in building and pollution is seen as crucial for future sustainability. With proper synergistic design, individual green building technologies may work together to produce a greater cumulative effect. MRCB has also introduced energy and water efficiency targets and implemented initiatives to reduce greenhouse gas emissions (GHG). We monitor our GHG emissions through a carbon footprint study. We continue to show our support towards the ‘Earth Hour’ initiative by turning off non-essential lights and other electrical appliances for one hour to raise awareness on climate change. Water usage is monitored and managed throughout the business. MRCB has created systems such as water usage and leak detection as well as efficient irrigation systems to encourage better use of resources. 35 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Water Withdrawal and Best Management Practice The data for green building developments (Lot E, Lot G and 348 Sentral) and MRCB Rehabilitation Projects (Tioman Island, Pahang and Kuantan River Mouth) is presented below. An Erosion and Sedimentation Control Plan (ESCP) is implemented on site to ensure that the surrounding drainage system is not adversely affected by our developments. A permanent silt trap was constructed and is being used at project sites. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 36 Policy on Waste Management The management of our waste is based on the national waste hierarchy which: • reduces the use of primary materials, prioritising those which damage health or give rise to hazardous waste • re-uses materials wherever possible • disposes of remaining waste in a responsible manner which is in compliance with the requirement of relevant licenses and other legal obligations In achieving this, MRCB has introduced its sustainable procurement and waste management policies which include: • Working with design teams and supply chains to use standard production timber sections for joinery to reduce unnecessary wastage • Reducing the transportation distance of construction materials by purchasing the materials with local suppliers • Insisting on reusable steel system formworks for concreting rather than timber plywood formworks to reduce timber and concrete nail waste. General waste (industrial, commercial and domestic waste) is controlled under the Local Government Act 1976 and Refuse Collection, Removal and Disposal By-Laws under the Act. The following mitigation measures are proposed for the handling of solid wastes potentially generated during the construction phase: • General municipal wastes are stored in containers and collected • Contractors are used to minimise odour, pest and litter impacts. • Scrap metals are recycled • No construction wastes can be burnt on site. Energy Efficiency and Conservation Construction sites involve processes which can be noisy, dusty and cause nuisance. We recognise that it is in our interests to plan activities to minimise these effects. We assess the environmental impact of activities on our construction sites and are energy efficient whenever possible. MRCB aims to conserve natural resources by minimising waste and encouraging the principles of reuse and recycling by engaging all staff and supply chain partners. We create energy efficient programmes and services that benefit our clients and the environment. Stesen Sentral Kuala Lumpur (SSKL) is MRCB’s flagship operation and the biggest transport hub in Malaysia, with a surface area of 87,539 m². Located just outside the centre of Kuala Lumpur, SSKL is fed by city buses, feeder coaches and taxis. Its rail network hub links all major rail systems in Peninsular Malaysia, including the KLIA Express, KLIA Transit, KTM Intercity, KTM Komuter, PUTRA LRT and the Kuala Lumpur Monorail system. A number of energy conservation tools are employed such as Chiller Optimisation Systems, Energy Monitoring and Saving Equipment and Energy Meter and Power Monitoring Systems. KPIs were set across the company to monitor energy usage and incorporate the energy efficiency target of 5 to 10%. This KPI includes both qualitative and quantitative indicators which enable us to benchmark our performance. It also identifies and shares best practices and covers all material issues such as energy efficiency and waste management. An Energy Management Team has been established at Group level, comprising an Energy Coordinator, Assistant Energy Coordinator, several Energy Supervisors and a Facilities and Maintenance Contractor. SSKL operates 24 hours a day. In order to manage energy consumption efficiently, SSKL has implemented an energy efficiency programme for the whole site since 2002. A Comprehensive Energy Efficiency programme was introduced in 2004, with the aim of resolving energy-related environmental problems, upgrading the quality of management and maximising the benefits of reduced energy consumption. This enhances competitiveness through savings from energy consumption costs. 37 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Energy Conservation and Efficiency Measures implemented to conserve energy include air conditioning control, lighting efficiency, green fixtures and fittings, energy efficient air conditioning and ventilation systems. MRCB has introduced Building Envelope Design Strategies as part of its Green Building structure which aim to achieve an average ETTV of 40W/m2 and lower. This strategy covers the use of external sun shading devices on the facade of buildings to minimise heat loading. It also covers the use of high performance low-E-glass and double-glazed insulated units. In 2007, MRCB adopted ‘paperless office’ practices, where employees are encouraged to use electronic documentation whenever possible. We also take initiatives to provide energy efficient lighting such as LED and T5 fittings. MRCB ensures that all its projects are energy efficient through the provision of green features such as motion sensors, a Heat Recovery Wheel and Ductless Mechanical Ventilation Systems. Programmes and Campaigns are being held to educate employees on the implementation of the energy saving programmes which include: • Switching off lights which are not in use • Encouraging employees to use sleep mode when computers are not in use • The identification, development and implementation of awareness programmes • Encouraging the use of recycled papers • Encouraging employees to practice dual side printing Distribution per system Transport 11% Lighting/Small Power Common Area 6% 6% Lighting/Small Power Retail 60% 17% Ventilation Air-Conditioning Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 38 Renewable Energy We have not been able to install alternative sources of energy in SSKL, as the building is owned by the Malaysian Ministry of Transport. However, we encourage this initiative through the provision of 1% replacement of electricity based on the total electricity consumption including tenants’ usage. Results and Achievements MRCB sets an energy conservation target of a 5% reduction in energy consumption each year from the baseline year of 2003. We achieved this target last year and again this year. In 2009, cumulative energy savings in MRCB were 20.3%. CARBON FOOTPRINT Biosphere Capital Pte Ltd (BC) has performed a carbon footprint assessment of MRCB premises around Kuala Lumpur Sentral development area. Both direct and indirect emissions have been included, to the extent possible given the data recorded during 2009. The greenhouse gas (GHG) assessment follows the ISO14064-1 standard and finds that the total equivalent carbon dioxide emissions are 16,075 tons/year during 2009. The objective of the GHG Assessment is to help devise a GHG reduction strategy and to prepare MRCB for compliance with climate regulations. The study also allows MRCB to manage its resources efficiently. Major emissions sources are: • Energy usage at MRCB offices • MRCB vehicle fleet • Work-related MRCB travel • Waste generated by MRCB office activities 39 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report MRCB’s emissions are found to be relatively small for a large company. In future compliance regime, the current cost of offsetting MRCB’s entire emissions using Voluntary Emissions Reductions (VERs) would be less than RM 0.4M/year. Our GHG Assessment is based on Financial Year 2009 and covers all operations under MRCB’s direct financial and operational control. Outsourced work is not covered. In accordance with the ISO standard, all direct energy and indirect energy use emissions are included. The GHG Assessment accounts for the following MRCB buildings and offices at Kuala Lumpur Sentral: 1. One Sentral : Four floors occupied by MRCB 2. One Sentral: Common areas managed by MRCB 3. Working together with energy and sustainable consultants, MRCB has appointed site managers to oversee each project area and is responsible for the entire environmental management and external accreditation such as Singapore’s BCA Greenmark, US-based Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design (LEED) and Malaysia’s Green Building Index. Our Approach to Green Building MRCB implemented two international environmental certifications in its property developments which are the Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design (LEED) and the Green Mark Certification. The LEED Green Building Rating System is a third party certification programme which encourages the global adoption of sustainable practices through universally accepted tools and performance criteria. The five key areas of human and environmental health covered by this certification are sustainable site development, water savings, energy savings, material selection and indoor environmental quality. The BCA Green Mark is a Singapore green building rating system which promotes sustainability in the construction of buildings. It pays particular attention to energy conservation and is endorsed and supported by the Singapore National Environment Agency. This approach acts as a stepping stone to the implementation and maintenance of a full Environmental Management System (EMS) and subsequently ISO 14001. During the initial submission, organisations are required to demonstrate their green practices in accordance with the Green Mark certification and organisations must comply with this level in order to retain this certification. 43 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report GREEN FEATURES ASSESSMENT Lot G Lot E 348 Sentral ENERGY EFFICIENT • All parking underground/ • Air-conditioning system uses a • Combination of green coatings within building District Cooling System and material with vegetated • Environmental Tobacco • Provision of Energy Efficient roof Smoke Control Lighting, such as LED and • Reduced heat gain through • Use of non-chlorofluorocarbons T5 fittings cool roof coating (CFC) refrigerant • Mechanical ventilation system • All site and building luminaries • CO2 level monitoring is coupled with CO sensors set at acceptable illuminance value ENVIRONMENT • Central storage and collection of • Singapore Green Label Scheme • Recycle corner on every PROTECTION non hazardous waste material (SGLS) and Green Star Certified office floor • Materials follow Volatile • Products with at least 30% • Wood based materials Organic Compound recycled content by weight/ certified by FSC principles (VOC) content limitation volume INDOOR • Construction Indoor Air Quality • Project uses low VOC paint • Comply with VOC Project ENVIRONMENT (IAQ) and Waste Management for all internal wall areas specification Carpet and Rug QUALITY Plan • Provision of high frequency Institute (CRI) Green Label ballast for all fluorescent Plus Programme luminaries WATER EFFICIENT • Water efficient fittings to • Use of Water Efficiency • All pavement is pervious for reduce water usage Labelling Scheme (WESLS). water removal • Water efficient fittings to reduce water usage; IMPACT ANALYSIS OF OUR GREEN BUILDING Return on Investment in Green Buildings MRCB has conducted an analysis of return on our major investments including Green Building Development to measure how efficiently we use our capital to generate profit. The results of this study have shown a clear relationship between green building investment and financial performance. The analysis projects the long term return on our green investment which we estimate saves RM3 per square foot compared to conventional non-green buildings. If we assume that the money saved is reallocated and a “hurdle rate,” which is a minimum required rate of return, the cumulative saving plus return will have grown to RM47.81 per square foot, after 10 years. After subtracting the assumed initial investment of RM8 per square foot, the total net benefit is RM39.81 which is an annual return of 39.76% per square foot for investing in green building projects compared to conventional projects of the same area. This investment varies according to the time horizon, hurdle rate, discount rate and other accounting assumptions. The results could vary if different methods had been followed. Incidents of Non-compliance MRCB records the total number of incidents of non-compliance with regulations and voluntary codes concerning the health and safety impacts within 24 months of delivery. Defects and complaints will then be responded to accordingly, for cases within the validity of warranty. Following 24 months of use and service, the group does not track any further effects of use, disposal or reuse as the properties involved frequently change ownership and the Group may not always be able to gain access. The Group did not have any major incidents of non-compliance with regulations, or its own voluntary codes concerning the health and safety impacts of its properties sold beyond the 30-day stage for fixing defects and addressing complaints. Investor Relations MRCB holds regular investor and analyst briefings as part of its Investor Relations (IR) initiatives in integrating two-way communication with the community and other constituencies. The main objective of this approach is to inform and update potential investors and current stakeholders on MRCB’s position in the current economic market and to gain further confidence in the company’s management. We aim to achieve a fair valuation at IR sessions. Our team comprises our Corporate Finance members and senior management who present business updates and business operational strategies. A total of 42 IR sessions were held in 2009 both locally and overseas (Las Vegas and Japan). This has resulted in a positive positioning for MRCB with its stock information being one of the most published in the Malaysian market. Customer Satisfaction Systems We conduct our Customer Satisfaction Surveys (CSS) on all residential and commercial properties that MRCB develops and manages. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 58 PINTAR Impact Analysis Prior to the final year of the programme in some schools, MRCB conducted a comprehensive study on the impact of this programme. Taking SK La Salle 1 Brickfields, as a sample school, results of the first examination and last examination of 2009 were compared and it was found that an improvement of 8% in students passing was achieved. The three core UPSR subjects English, Maths and Science have shown an increase by 11.3 %, 12.3% and 5.7% respectively compared to the previous year. During 2009, MRCB conducted dialogue sessions with the direct stakeholders involved in the programme including principals of the schools, teachers, students and parents. Students are delighted with the PINTAR contribution and found it helpful to their studies as well as their personal development. As students in these schools are mostly from lower-income families, the PINTAR programme enables them to gain better access to academic resources and assistance in the form of extra classes or motivational trips, which were not readily available to them before the implementation of this programme. Students and principals believe that facilities, infrastructure and extra hours dedicated from the programme have contributed towards a better understanding of the subjects covered. A study trip that was part of the programme covers academic-related topics and lessons on attitude and behaviour. Intensive classes were held for standard 6 students prior to the Primary School Achievement Test (UPSR). In 2009, these intensive classes were conducted in the second half of the academic year. Two study trips were conducted in the same year, covering three days of interactive sessions. The programme aims to provide students with a unique study experience in different settings. We received positive feedback from students and parents about these courses which covers both academic and non-academic related topics. A lack of parents’ participation was identified after the second year as a majority of students in these schools came from dual-income parents. It is difficult for parents to attend these meetings. Only 14 out of 57 parents were present at the Parents Teachers meeting. 59 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report PINTAR This year MRCB experimented with the Social Return on Investment (SROI) method to measure the impact of our PINTAR programme. SROI is a framework for measuring and accounting the value of investment by incorporating social, environmental and economic costs and benefits. For the purpose of this analysis, SK La Salle 1, Brickfields is taken as our sample study, due to the amount of data available. The data obtained from the school on the number of pass students in every examination can be seen below: Subject Number of Start Year End Year Candidates Examination Examination Pemahaman 57 42 48 Penulisan 57 38 44 English 57 41 37 Mathematics 57 23 31 Science 57 28 34 The passing rate for the beginning of the year examination was compared to the examination held at the end of the year. It has shown an average increase of 4.4 students passing the examination. The analysis covers the period of three years. We estimate that there is RM2.33 of social value added in every RM1 spent on our investment in the PINTAR programme in this school. The SROI varies according to time horizons, tax, savings rates and other accounting assumptions. This is based on the assumption that all other circumstances remain the same over the three years of the calculation. We strive to eliminate discrimination based on culture, nationality, religion, creed, race, gender, age, physical ability and others. We also endeavour to preserve the dignity of each individual employee and create a healthy workplace for everyone. Policy on Workplace Relations MRCB’s grievance policy states that any one person does not arbitrarily make decisions which will be prejudicial to the interests of the employees and the Company. Our Grievance Procedure allows employees to voice their problems or complaints to higher levels of management. The purpose of the procedure is to settle the grievance as near as possible to the point of origin. In any event, an employee is encouraged to discuss the grievance with his immediate superior first. If he fails to get a satisfactory response he may make use of the appeal procedures. Local Hiring Policies for Senior Managers The Group specifically recruits Malaysians for senior management positions within Malaysia. Currently, all senior management positions (Vice-President and above) are held by Malaysians. Career Development for Employees MRCB continues to grow and place emphasis on attracting and retaining Malaysian talent to the company. The budget allocated for training in 2009 was RM1,510 per employee. We believe that our employees are our greatest assets and crucial to our continued success as a developer. Our workplace practices and policies reflect this and we are committed to investing in our employees’ training and career development, as far as is possible. This includes internal training programmes and inter-departmental team building programmes which are designed to develop individual initiatives, interpersonal skills and the technical competence of employees. MRCB employees are encouraged to go for formal certification such as a diploma or degree to foster the next generation of leaders and provide better employability opportunities. We continue to enhance this programme as part of our commitment to the systematic middle-to-long-range development of Human Resources. Currently, the Group does not have any training policies relating to retirees. Regular Reviews of Employee Performance and Career Development We recognise the importance of understanding our employees’ need. As part of our employees’ career management framework, we continue to conduct our formal appraisal system for all full-time employees which are conducted twice a year. This evaluation system intends to bring out the best in our employees and to prepare them for greater roles and responsibilities within the organisation. This evaluation also acts as guidance for our remuneration system which is used in pay increment, promotion and bonus decisions. In 2009, 88% of MRCB’s employees received a formal performance evaluation at least once each year. Please refer to the performance data tables at the end of this report for a detailed breakdown. Average Hours of Training per Year per Employee We prioritise our Human Resources system and training programmes to provide diverse opportunities that aid our employees’ career advancement. Our training sessions ensure complete understanding of their role and rights including a career enhancement path for our staff. Total training hours during 2009 were 8,350 (84%) for managers and 1,600 (16%) for non-managerial staff. This is an average of 13.51 and 3.01 training hours per employee, for managerial and non-managerial staff respectively. 69 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report We conducted our team building programmes first in 2006 which are now an integral part of our company structure. This programme aims to nurture interpersonal skills and technical competence for both management and supporting staff. We also give top priority to professional ethical training, strengthening the content of programmes, while providing ongoing ethics education. In order to measure the effectiveness of this programme, we conducted a survey to gauge employee job satisfaction and the level to which their training and career development programmes fulfil their needs. This survey is anonymous and is conducted by independent consultants every alternate year. The 2008 survey results show that two-thirds of employees surveyed believed the team building programme had helped them feel a sense of company pride and loyalty. 62.74% considered their people skills had improved as a result of the programme. 56.78% considered these exercises have helped MRCB develop a new working culture. Impact Analysis on the Provision of Employee Benefits The cost of providing employees with a wide variety of fringe benefits is considered a tax deductible business expense for employers. As many of these benefits are not classed as employees’ income, they also receive tax incentives. Expenses which are considered ordinary, reasonable and necessary to the business can be tax deductible which includes group insurance, medical benefits and surgical costs for MRCB. This can be subtracted from our income before it is taxed. The reduction of taxable income minimises our tax liability and improves our bottom line. Collective Bargaining Agreements At MRCB, 53.8% of total staff are executive grade and above. Under Malaysian law it is not a usual practice for executive staff to have a union. 46.2% of total employees are non-executive staff at the end of 2009 and are very widely distributed among the 21 active subsidiaries of the Group. It has not been considered beneficial for them to have a group-wide union and the relatively low number of non-executive staff throughout Group companies and subsidiaries does not carry the critical mass that would justify the establishment of such a body. The Group Human Resources Manual has codified procedures and processes available for all employees to engage collectively and air grievances and protect employees’ rights. Notice Period for Operational Change Any restructuring of operations are done with consultations with managerial and supervisory employees. The impact of the changes is also assessed when appropriate. If the company makes operational changes that potentially affect our employees, we have a policy of giving a minimum of two weeks notice to the staff. The more significant the operational change, the longer the period of notice given. 71 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Our quarterly newsletter, the “Resources” is one of our methods Human Rights in nurturing effective dialogue with our staff members. formally appraised at least once annually (updated) 88 89.4 87.5% 88.9% 81.1% 77 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Notes on Data Collation and Presentation The compilation and presentation of this report is according to GRI-G3 Guidelines. We considered the limitations in the availability of data or in the case where stakeholders cannot be involved or the availability of any form of reportable information in our reporting process. For our 2009 Sustainability Report, we have put our utmost effort on disclosure and in reporting all information we have as comprehensively as possible. Where there are gaps in the data, we have classified these as “partially reported”. This is especially in the Environmental Section, as we do not have systems established to monitor some indicators. In cases where we are not able to provide detailed figures, we have included aggregate information which we consider to be representative of our approach and performance. This is particularly in the Environmental Section where greenhouse gas data comes from Stesen Sentral Kuala Lumpur Sdn Bhd. We consider this to be the most material environmental information for the Group due to its coverage, consistency and time range. We aim to improve our data collection systems in the following year so that we can achieve a more consistent environmental data for all of our operations in future reports. With regards to GHG Emissions, we have applied the GHG Protocol 2004 recommended by GRI from the World Council for Sustainable Business Development and the World Resources Initiative. We are not able to report on specific areas of EN10, EN19, EN21, EN23, and EN24 as we do not have sufficient supporting data on these cases. We have also not reported on the percentage of products and packaging reclaimed (EN27) as this is not directly relevant to the nature of our operations as a construction company. We have disclosed our environmental expenditures (EN30) partially and we are in the process of developing our data collection systems for our next report. The collection of information is also provided by our sub-contractors for most of our projects and so MRCB does not hold the full responsibility for this information. The development of these systems is given priority in our 2010-2011 Group Agenda. Subject to the success of this review, we expect to be able to provide more comprehensive information after these processes have been fully implemented. This report has shown an improvement compared to previous sustainability reports with better disclosure of quantitative and qualitative data. We have provided a Disclosure on Management Approach (DMA) in each of the categories and profile disclosures. We are able to provide full or partial data on 114 out of 120 Performance Indicators. We believe the remaining 6 indicators do not influence the overall CSR assessment of the company. We were engaged by Malaysian Resources Corporation Berhad (“MRCB”) to provide assurance services for their Sustainability Report 2009 (the “Report”). The Report and its contents are the exclusive responsibility of MRCB. Our responsibility is to perform limited assurance procedures over the Report and underlying processes within the scope set out below: • Economic Verification through low-level assurance via information provided by MRCB including verification of calculations for the presentation of Economic Value-Added using independently audited data from MRCB Annual Reports • Social Performance: Labour Practices & Decent Work Verification to a low level assurance via information presented by MRCB and presentation to internationally recognised reporting standards • Social Performance: Human Rights Verification through low-level assurance via information provided by MRCB • Social Performance: Society Verification through low-level assurance via information provided by MRCB • Social Performance: Product Responsibility Verification to a low level assurance via information provided by MRCB • Environmental Verification through low-level assurance via information provided by MRCB including verification of calculations and application of international protocols for the presentation of CO2 emissions (EN16, EN17 & EN18) It is agreed that MRCB expects to be able to provide a response to each of the GRI-G3 Guideline Protocols and to provide an A+ or Advanced Application Level which requires reporting on each of the GRI-G3 indicators, even if the report is an omission statement. Exclusions from the scope of our work Excluded from the scope of our work is information relating to: • Statements of commitment or intention to undertake action in the future; • Statements of opinion, belief or aspiration; • Information in internal or external documents referred to in the Report, except insofar as we have viewed their existence as part of the assurance process Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 86 Basis of our opinion In conducting this engagement we have considered the principles of balance, comparability, accuracy, timeliness, clarity, relevance and reliability as in the Global Reporting Initiative (GRI) G3 Guidelines. We have also taken into account the principles of independence of assurance in the GRI-G3 Guidelines and have been mindful of the AA1000AS and the International Standard on Assurance Engagements (ISAE 3000) although we have not been asked to apply these standards directly. We have conducted this engagement to provide a reasonable rather than an absolute level of assurance and we believe that the work conducted and described herein provides a reasonable basis for our conclusions. Our review included the following activities: • Interviews and one-to-one meetings with relevant personnel at corporate and operation level responsible for the information in the Report; • Interviews and one-to-one meetings with relevant external stakeholders related to MRCB activities, including three separate architects for each MRCB Green Building projects, headmistress, students and representatives of the Parent-Teachers Association of MRCB PINTAR project schools; • Documentary evidence was reviewed from communications meant for both internal and external circulation but emanating from within MRCB. This comprised of manually generated internal reports, reports generated from internal specialist management information systems, established codes of conduct including the Code of Ethics (2004) and the Prevention of Fraud Manual 2006, operating manuals, internal newsletters and the annual audited financial reports of MRCB; • Observed related facilities and areas including notice boards, management offices; • Review of a Greenhouse Gas Assessment (GHG) Report provided by Biosphere Capital Pte Ltd; • A review of figures for all direct and indirect greenhouse gas (CO2) emissions and reductions (EN16, 17 & 18) as well as for economic value generated (EC 1) to ascertain the accuracy of the calculation of the figures reported; and • Challenges to the CSR related statements and claims made in the Report; During our investigation we discussed the necessary changes in the Report with MRCB personnel and determined that these changes have been adequately incorporated into the final version. We relied on representations made to us during the course of our assurance work by MRCB personnel. Information in the Report that is directly sourced from MRCB Annual reports is considered to be reliable based on the audit statement of the Independent Chartered Accountant and Registered Auditor to these statements. We provided advice on which data is necessary and how this data should be compiled to comply with the GRIG3 Guidelines. All data and correction were provided directly by MRCB staff. In the same reporting period we have provided a separate internal study and some parts of which may have been used in this report. We do not consider the information used to be of significant or material importance and its inclusion does not conflict with the independence of our opinion. Conclusions 1. In our opinion, the Report meets the content and quality requirements of the Global Reporting Initiative Sustainability Reporting Guidelines (Version G-3); 2. The Report provides a fair representation of MRCB’s social accounting and reporting activity for the period covered by the Report; 3. The information in the Report is reliable and free from significant bias; 4. MRCB has processes in place for identifying, understanding and managing its environmental and social responsibilities and for capturing, understanding and responding to the views of its main stakeholders; and 5. In our opinion the report contains new information in each domain which we believe is a fair and balanced reflection of the efforts of MRCB to develop and improve their approach to sustainability and reporting. 87 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Recommendations: In the context of future CSR Reporting at MRCB, we recommend that the company: • Continues to improve the use of performance indicators; • Continues to improve the scope and quality of measurement and reporting of environmental data especially in water usage; • Introduces clearer links between CSR issues and financial performance; • Extends the use of impact measures such as Social Return on Investment (SROI) and Environmental Return on Investment (EROI); • Implements GHG reduction programmes to reduce overall GHG equivalent emissions from the 2009 baseline estimate provided in this report; and • Introduces processes for the ongoing monitoring, measurement and reporting of MRCB against material indicators and targets to demonstrate ongoing commitment to the reporting process and stakeholder interests. Considerations and limitations In relation to our assurance work and conclusions, the following considerations and limitations should be noted: • Certain information is excluded from the scope of our assurance work, as stated above and in the Report itself; • Due to its nature and the methods used for determining, calculating or estimating such data, environmental and social data are subject to inherent limitations. Therefore this assurance statement should not be relied upon to detect all errors, omissions or misstatements in the Report; and • The assurance statement cannot guarantee the quality of social accounting and reporting processes used by MRCB. This is the third year in which we have conducted assurance of MRCB’s Sustainability Report. In accordance with our Code of Conduct on Assurance and Assessment we have advised MRCB to explore alternative assurance options for the next reporting period. This three year rotation process is intended to promote the ongoing independence of the assurance process. 31st March 2010 OWW Consulting Sdn Bhd Dr Geoffrey Williams Chief Executive Officer Statement by OWW Consulting Sdn Bhd on Independence, Objectivity and Capability OWW Consulting Sdn Bhd (OWW) is a specialist in Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR) and Socially Responsible Investment (SRI) with established experience in providing independent CSR advisory, reporting and assurance services. OWW Consulting has implemented a Code of Conduct in Assurance and Assessment and a Code of Ethics across our company. Our Code requires that that all of our employees maintain high ethical standards and makes explicit reference to the independence and objectivity of our assurance and assessment engagements which we believe conform to emerging international best practice. Our assurance team conducting the work for this report have experience in conducting engagements of this type for sustainability reports, systems and processes. They are familiar with current guidelines and best practice and update their experience on a regular basis. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 88 Linking bridge at Tekek, Tioman Island 89 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Penyata KETUA PEGAWAI EKSEKUTIF Mohamed Razeek Hussain MARICAR Ketua Pegawai Eksekutif Bagi pihak ahli Lembaga Pengarah, saya dengan sukacitanya membentangkan Laporan Mapan MRCB bagi tahun ini yang menekankan sumbangan kami terhadap pembangunan mapan dan tindakan kami yang memberi kesan ke atas kumpulan pemegang kepentingan utama kami – pelanggan, pemegang saham, warga kerja, rakan kongsi, masyarakat dan alam sekitar amnya. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 90 Tahun lepas merupakan tahun yang begitu penting bagi MRCB. Kami komited untuk memberikan prestasi cemerlang sebagai salah satu daripada pemaju hartanah perumahan, komersil dan perindustrian yang terbesar di Malaysia. Saya berasa gembira kerana walaupun berhadapan dengan kesukaran ekonomi, hala tuju dan visi Kumpulan yang strategik telah membantu kami mencapai matlamat perniagaan dan Tanggungjawab Sosial Korporat (CSR). Bagi tahun ini, kami telah berjaya mencatat keuntungan sebanyak RM921.6 juta, iaitu meningkat sebanyak 17% dari tempoh kewangan sebelumnya. Pencapaian kami diiktiraf apabila MRCB memenangi anugerah dalam tiga kategori pada Anugerah Laporan Mapan ACCA Malaysia 2009 (ACCA MaSRA) – “Laporan Prestasi Alam Sekitar Terbaik”, “Pengiktirafan Khas – Pendekatan Jaminan”, dan finalis bagi anugerah keseluruhan. MRCB adalah antara dua finalis teratas bagi Anugerah CSR Perdana Menteri 2009 bagi Kategori Kebudayaan dan Warisan dan juga terpilih sebagai finalis di Anugerah Tanggungjawab Sosial Korporat StarBiz 2009 dalam Kategori Pasaran. MRCB terus diiktiraf oleh National Annual Corporate Report Awards (NACRA) pada tahun 2009 dan telah memenangi Anugerah Perak bagi Laporan Tanggungjawab Sosial Korporat Terbaik. Perniagaan hartanah MRCB di Sooka Sentral telah menerima pengiktirafan dalam Anugerah Hartanah FIABCI Malaysia 2009 dalam kategori Pembangunan Binaan Khas. Bekas Pengarah Urusan Kumpulan kami, Shahril Ridza Ridzuan telah dinamakan sebagai Ketua Pegawai Eksekutif Hartanah 2009 oleh FIABCI Malaysia. Ini membuktikan bahawa MRCB telah mencapai kejayaan besar sebagai sebuah Kumpulan. MRCB mewakili sebagai ahli jawatankuasa bagi Malaysia ke United Nations Global Compact (UNGC) Malaysia dalam usaha mencapai sasaran kami untuk mengguna pakai piawaian antarabangsa bagi program dan visi CSR kami. Matlamat kami adalah untuk menggabungkan kesemua 10 prinsip UNGC yang merangkumi hak asasi manusia, hak pekerja, kemapanan alam sekitar dan anti-rasuah dalam operasi dan strategi syarikat dan juga untuk melaporkan pelaksanaannya. Kami menyokong dan berikrar untuk terus mematuhi 10 prinsip universal tentang hak asasi manusia, hak pekerja, kemapanan alam sekitar dan anti rasuah. 91 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Komitmen Terhadap Pendedahan Yang Lebih Baik dan Ketelusan Laporan Kami telah dapat mengekalkan prestasi cemerlang kami dalam laporan selepas mencapai Aplikasi Tahap A+ selaras dengan rangka kerja Initiatif Laporan Global (GRI-G3) bagi Laporan Mapan. Penilaian bebas oleh GRI di Amsterdam telah mengesahkan bahawa MRCB telah membuat laporan tentang kesemua petunjuk utama yang diperlukan di bawah GRI-G3 yang mengukur tahap pendedahan dan ketelusan dalam amalan perniagaan. Dalam tempoh laporan ini, kami telah dapat menyediakan maklumat tambahan dalam bidang yang sebelum ini kurang dilaporkan, termasuklah pendedahan tentang tahap pelepasan yang ketara, kesan pengangkutan produk ke atas alam sekitar, sistem tadbir urus program alam sekitar MRCB, senarai-senarai sistem pengurusan mapan yang lain dan data perakaunan sosial dan alam sekitar. Inisiatif Alam Sekitar MRCB merupakan peneraju dalam bidang kejuruteraan alam sekitar di Malaysia dan telah terlibat dalam pemulihan pantai, sungai dan pesisir pantai. Selaras dengan Rancangan Malaysia Kesembilan, MRCB terus memainkan peranan yang aktif dalam pengawalan banjir, pemulihan, pengurusan perparitan dan memerangi isu alam sekitar yang lain. Pada tahun 2009, MRCB telah menyiapkan projek pemulihan di Pulau Tioman yang menelan belanja sebanyak RM132 juta. Analisis terperinci tentang kesan projek ini telah dijalankan dan hasilnya didedahkan di bahagian Alam Sekitar laporan ini. Kami telah meneruskan usaha kami dengan menggabungkan isu-isu alam sekitar ke dalam bahagian-bahagian perniagaan yang lain. Inisiatif ini merangkumi projek pengurusan binaan kami yang disertakan sebagai Petunjuk Prestasi Utama (KPI). MRCB komited dalam memainkan peranan sebagai sebuah syarikat Malaysia dengan menyumbang kepada Matlamat Hijau Malaysia. Kami merasa bangga menjadi peneraju Indeks Bangunan Hijau bagi Malaysia untuk projek-projek pembangunan sedia ada dan yang akan datang melalui inisiatif bangunan hijau dan amalan terbaik seperti pensijilan Leadership in Energy and Environment Design (LEED) yang dikeluarkan oleh US Green Building Council; Building and Construction Authority (BCA) Green Mark, Singapura dan Indeks Bangunan Hijau (GBI) Malaysia. Strategi ini telah dilaksanakan di dalam kesemua projek baru yang dijalankan di mercu tanda ikonik kami iaitu pembangunan Kuala Lumpur Sentral – 348 Sentral, Lot G dan Lot E. Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report 92 Kumpulan juga telah melaksanakan Pelan Pengurusan Alam Kami komited untuk memantau prestasi alam sekitar bagi Sekitar (EMP) untuk memantau kesan operasi kami terhadap bangunan-bangunan di bawah pengurusan kami. Dengan alam sekitar. Kami telah mewujudkan Sistem Pengurusan Alam sukacitanya, kami ingin melaporkan tentang kejayaan berterusan Sekitar (EMS) untuk menguruskan semua aspek prestasi alam sistem kami di Stesen Sentral Kuala Lumpur, hab pengangkutan sekitar termasuklah pelepasan, kualiti marin dan air, penggunaan awam utama di ibu negara. Kami telah berjaya mencapai bahan dan pengurangan tenaga dan sisa. Langkah ini meletakkan pengurangan dalam penggunaan tenaga sebanyak 20.3% pada penekanan yang ketara ke atas kesan projek kami dan hasilnya tahun 2009, dan ini adalah melebihi sasaran tahunan kami iaitu dilaporkan di bahagian Alam Sekitar laporan ini. sebanyak 5%. Kami juga telah menjalankan kempen kesedaran bersama WWF Malaysia dengan menggunakan poster bagi menggalakkan penyewa di bangunan kami menyokong kempen tersebut. Kempen ini dianjurkan oleh MRCB di 1 Sentral, Sooka Sentral, Plaza Sentral, Stesen Sentral, dan Plaza Alam Sentral. Pada tahun 2009, buat kali pertama, kami telah menjalankan penyelidikan mengenai Gas Rumah Hijau (GHG). Tujuan penyelidikan ini adalah untuk membangunkan strategi mengurangkan GHG berdasarkan pelepasan karbon kami yang terkini. Kewarganegaraan Korporat Saya juga dengan sukacitanya ingin melaporkan bahawa kami telah melipat-gandakan usaha untuk mewujudkan nilai perkongsian untuk masyarakat dengan memfokuskan kepada projek-projek Tanggungjawab Korporat berhubung Komuniti, Pasaran dan Alam Sekitar. Pada tahun 2009, kami telah melaburkan sejumlah RM1.5 juta dalam projek komuniti kami. Ini akan menguatkan komitmen kami untuk mewujudkan nilai perkongsian bukan sahaja untuk pemegang saham, tetapi juga komuniti secara keseluruhannya. MRCB komited untuk memelihara hubungan yang nyata antara kami dengan pemegang saham dan inisiatif CSR kami adalah penggabungan dengan strategi perniagaan dan jenama. Enam buah sekolah telah diambil sebagai sekolah angkat di bawah program MRCB PINTAR pada tahun 2009. Sekolah-sekolah tersebut adalah SK La Salle 1 dan SK La Salle 2, di Brickfields, Kuala Lumpur, SK Tebrau Bakar Batu di Johor Bahru dan SK Bagan Jermal dan SK Kampong Jawa di Pulau Pinang. Tahun ini merupakan tahun akhir bagi program tiga tahun sekolah angkat PINTAR bagi dua daripada sekolah tersebut. Saya berasa gembira dengan keputusan dan maklum balas positif yang telah kami terima. Kami percaya bahawa anakanak adalah masa depan kita dan menjadi tanggungjawab kita untuk menyediakan mereka dengan tahap persediaan terbaik dalam perjalanan pendidikan mereka. Kami telah meningkatkan usaha kami untuk memperkayakan komuniti di mana kami beroperasi dan telah mengambil langkah kawalan untuk mengurangkan kesan negatif dan menekankan kesan positif aktiviti pembinaan kami ke atas komuniti tempatan. Sebagai contoh, kami mematuhi dan mengatasi peraturan kebangsaan mengenai tahap kebisingan, gegaran, debu dan pelbagai isu alam sekitar yang lain. 93 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report Di dalam Pasaran, kami masih meneruskan untuk mempromosi amalan perniagaan yang baik di seluruh Syarikat. Asas kejayaan kami adalah Tanggungjawab Korporat yang baik. Kami akan melakukan yang terbaik untuk memainkan peranan kami sebagai Warga Korporat contoh. Inisiatif di Tempat Kerja Penghargaan yang sewajarnya perlu diberi kepada warga kerja kami yang telah bekerja keras untuk menjana keuntungan dan memastikan bahawa petunjuk kewangan lain berada di paras yang kukuh. Kami sedang mengimbangi antara objektif jangka pendek dan jangka panjang untuk mencapai pertumbuhan yang stabil dan mapan. Ini memastikan pulangan yang menguntungkan kepada pemegang saham kami walaupun dalam keadaan operasi yang mencabar. Pada tahun 2009, kami terus melabur dalam program-program latihan untuk warga kerja bagi mengembangkan bakat dan menyediakan mereka untuk menghadapi cabaran yang lebih hebat di tempat kerja. Kami sedar bahawa warga kerja kami adalah aset penting Cabaran bagi kami untuk menangani peningkatan permintaan bagi syarikat dan kami juga percaya kepada pembelajaran dalam pasaran yang sedang berkembang dan penumpuan sepanjang hayat kepada mereka. MRCB telah meneruskan terhadap isu-isu alam sekitar global, seperti perubahan iklim, usaha untuk melabur dalam pembangunan sumber manusia semuanya merupakan isu penting bagi perniagaan kami. bagi meningkatkan tahap daya laksana kerja mereka. Sebagai sebahagian daripada agenda masa hadapan, kami akan memberikan tumpuan yang lebih besar untuk menempatkan Yayasan MRCB pada kedudukan strategik di dalam Kumpulan. Isu-isu penting adalah “topik dan petunjuk yang kesan yang besar ke atas operasi kami dan juga kebimbangan mencerminkan kesan ekonomi, persekitaran dan sosial pemegang kepentingan, kami telah merumuskan pendekatan organisasi, atau yang akan mempengaruhi penilaian dan bagi laporan mapan. Laporan ini telah disusun supaya ia keputusan pemegang kepentingan”. menekankan bidang-bidang keutamaan, mengemukakan rasional bagi setiap pilihan dan menunjukkan komitmen kami Dalam membentuk rangka kerja kemapanan, kami telah dalam menangani setiap bidang dan prestasi terkini. mengguna pakai Garis Panduan GRI-G3 berhubung Laporan Kemapanan. Usaha kemapanan kami telah diberikan struktur Kami berusaha gigih untuk meningkatkan pendedahan dengan dengan pelaksanaan analisis kepentingan. Ini membolehkan menggunakan borang proksi untuk sistem laporan bagi pengenalpastian isu-isu kesan sosial dan persekitaran mendapatkan konteks tersembunyi bagi data. Sebagai contoh, yang disebabkan oleh operasi kami dan penilaian terhadap arah aliran data prestasi di dalam sektor ini kadang kala tidak kepentingannya kepada pemegang kepentingan. Maklum dapat diperolehi kerana sesetengah data dianggap sulit dan balas kami terhadap isu-isu juga dihadkan oleh tahap kawalan rahsia. Dalam kes-kes sebegitu, data penanda aras yang boleh atau kemampuan kami untuk mempengaruhi keputusan dasar didapati digunakan bagi menggantikan data sektor tertentu. dan amalan. Dalam kes kecekapan dan pemantauan air, kami masih belum memasang sebarang sistem untuk mengumpul maklumat Mengenal Pasti Isu Utama yang diperlukan. Merujuk kepada pemetaan kepentingan kami, isu-isu ini telah dikenal pasti, dikaji semula dan diluluskan Kami telah cuba untuk melaksanakan proses mengenal oleh pihak pengurusan kanan sebagai sebahagian daripada pasti isu-isu utama mengikut tiga kategori umum yang telah komitmen kami yang berterusan ke arah kemapanan. ditentukan oleh GRI-G3 – Ekonomi, Sosial dan Alam Sekitar. Dari sudut perniagaan kami, kebanyakan isu mempunyai kaitan yang jelas dengan kesan ekonomi, sosial dan alam sekitar. Kami mengklasifikasikan isu-isu tersebut mengikut bidang yang berkemungkinan akan terjejas. Nilai Potensi Kesan Isu dan Kepentingannya Kepada Pemegang Kepentingan Pemegang kepentingan kami merangkumi pemegang kepentingan dalaman dan luaran. Kumpulan pemegang kepentingan dalaman terbesar adalah warga kerja kami. Kumpulan pemegang kepentingan luaran yang utama adalah pemegang saham, pelanggan, rakan kongsi rantaian nilai dan komuniti yang tinggal di kawasan di mana kami beroperasi. Kami belum menjalankan pelaksanaan penglibatan pemegang kepentingan yang komprehensif tetapi pada tahun 2009, kami telah mula mengumpul maklum balas dan cadangan pemegang kepentingan terhadap proses pengurusan mapan seperti program PINTAR. 97 Laporan Tanggungjawab Korporat 2009 Sustainability Report PEMETAAN PEMEGANG KEPENTINGAN MRCB dan Pemegang Kepentingan Kami MRCB berusaha untuk menyertakan kesemua pemegang kepentingan di dalam operasi perniagaannya. Kami percaya bahawa adalah menjadi tugas kami untuk menangani keperluan pemegang kepentingan kami, terutamanya dalam menjayakan aktiviti CSR kami. Kami menggalakkan dialog yang aktif antara MRCB dan pemegang kepentingan, dan juga antara kumpulan pemegang kepentingan. Kami berusaha untuk menghadapi pelbagai cabaran secara proaktif dan mengadakan komunikasi yang telus.
